### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's represent Joe's age as "J", Joe's sister's age as "S", and Joe's father's age as "F".
  We know that J + S + F = 100.
  We know that when Joe is as old as his father, their ages will be equal, so J + F = 2F, which simplifies to J = F.
  We also know that when this happens, Joe's sister will be twice as old as she is now, so S + (F - S) * 2 = 2S, which simplifies to F = 3S.
  We can use this information to create two equations with two variables:
    J + S + F = 100
    F = 3S
  Solving this system of equations, we get:
    J = 25
    S = 25
    F = 75
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Let's define:
  Joe's age as J
  Joe's sister's age as S
  Joe's father's age as F

From the problem statement, we have two equations:
  J + S + F = 100     (Equation 1)
  J + (2*S) = F       (Equation 2)

We need to find F. 

Let's solve the problem by elimination method:
  Multiplying Equation 2 by 2, we get
  2J + 4S = 2F        (Equation 3)
  
  Subtracting Equation 2 from Equation 1, we get
  S + F = 100 - J     (Equation 4)
  
  Subtracting Equation 4 from Equation 3, we get
  2J + 3S = J + F     (Equation 5)
  
  Substitute Equation 2 into Equation 5, we get
  2J + 3S = J + 2S
  J = S
  
  Substitute J=S into Equation 1, we get
  2J + F = 100
  F = 100 - 2J
  
  Substitute J=S into Equation 2, we get
  3J = F
  F = 3J
  
  Equating the two expressions for F, we get
  100 - 2J = 3J
  5J = 100
  J = 20

  Therefore,
  F = 3J = 3*20 = 60

Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:

  - When Joe is as old as his father, we know that x + z = 2(y+ z-x) --> x+z = 2y + 2z - 2x --> 3x - 2y - z = 0
  - When Joe is as old as his father, we also know that z = 2(y - z + x)
     --> 2z = 2y + 2x --> z - y - x = 0
Action:

  Solving these equations, we will get x = 22, y = 28, and z = 50.

Response 3:
Let's start by assigning variables to the different ages:
Let Joe's age be J, Joe's sister's age be S, and Joe's father's age be F.

From the first piece of information, we know that:
J + S + F = 100

From the second piece of information, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. This means that the age difference between Joe and his sister will always be twice the difference between Joe and his father:
(J - F) = 2(S - J)

Simplifying this equation:
3J - 2S + F = 0

From the third piece of information, we know that when Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. This means that the age difference between Joe's father and Joe will always be twice the age difference between Joe's father and Joe's sister:
(F - J) = 2(F - S)

Simplifying this equation:
J + S = F

We can now substitute J + S with F in the first equation:
J + S + F = 100
J + S + J + S = 100
2J + 2S = 100
J + S = 50

We can now substitute J + S with F in the third equation:
J + S = F
50 = F

Therefore, Joe's father is 50 years old.

Response 6:
Let's start with the age of Joe's sister.
Let's assume Joe's age is j, Joe's sister's age is s, and Joe’s father's age is f.

From the first statement, we have:
j + s + f = 100  ----(1)

From the second statement, we know that when Joe is the same age as his father, his sister will be twice as old as she is now. Let's assume that x is the number of years until Joe is the same age as his father.

Then, we have:
j + x = f + x
j = f

Also, we know that when Joe is the same age as his father, his sister will be twice as old as she is now:
2*(s+x) = s

Simplifying the above equation, we get:
s = 2x

From the third statement, we know that when Joe is the same age as his father, his father is twice as old as his sister was when she was the same age as her father. Let's assume that y is the number of years until Joe is the same age as his father:

Then, we have:
f + y = 2*(s-y)
f + y = 2*(2x-y)
f + y = 4x - 2y

Simplifying the above equation, we get:
f = 3x - y

Now we have three equations with three unknowns. We can solve for them:
j + s + f = 100  ----(1)
j = f
s = 2x
f = 3x - y

Substituting j = f, s = 2x, and f = 3x - y into equation (1), we get:
j + s + f = 100
f + 2x + f = 100
2f + 2x = 100
2(3x - y) + 2x = 100
8x - 2y = 100
4x - y = 50

Now we have two equations with two unknowns. We can solve for them:
s = 2x
f = 3x - y
4x - y = 50
y = 4x - 50

Substituting y = 4x - 50 into f = 3x - y, we get:
f = 3x - (4x - 50)
f = 50 - x

Now we know the age of Joe's father is 50 - x. We need to find the value of x to solve for f.

Substituting y = 4x - 50 into 4x - y = 50, we get:
4x - (4x - 50) = 50
50 = 50

This is true for any value of x. Therefore, we can choose any value of x to solve for f.

Let's choose x = 8. Then, y = 22 and f = 42.

Therefore, the age of Joe's father is 42.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  For every head flipped, Jonathan receives $2 and for every tail flipped, Christopher receives $3. 
  After 20 coin flips, none of them won or lost any amount, which means they won or lost the same amount of money.
  If x is the number of times the coin landed on heads, then the number of times the coin landed on tails is 20 - x.
  The total amount of money exchanged is 2x - 3(20 - x) = 0.
  Solving for x gives: 5x = 60, x = 12.

Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Every time a head comes up, Christopher gives Jonathan $2.
  Every time a tail comes up, Jonathan gives Christopher $3.
  After 20 flips, neither won or lost any amount.
  We want to find out how many times the coin landed on heads.
Solution:
  Let's say the coin landed on heads "h" times and tails "t" times.
  We know that h + t = 20 (because there were 20 flips in total).
  We also know that 2h = 3t (because for every head, Christopher gives $2 and for every tail, Jonathan gives $3; but since they both won/lost the same amount, we can equate the two sides).
  Rearranging the second equation, we get h = (3/2)t.
  Substituting this into the first equation, we get (3/2)t + t = 20.
  Solving for t, we get t = 8.
  Therefore, h = (3/2)t = (3/2)(8) = 12.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  - When the coin lands on heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
  - When the coin lands on tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  - After 20 coin flips, neither of them won or lost any money.
  - Let x be the number of times the coin landed on heads.
Action: 
  - If the coin landed on heads x times, Christopher gave away $2x.
  - If the coin landed on tails (20-x) times, Jonathan gave away $3(20-x) = $60 - $3x.
  - Since no one won or lost any money, $2x = $60 - $3x.
  - Solving for x gives x = 12.
Answer: Answer("E")

Response 8:
Knowledge:
- For each Heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
- For each Tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
- After 20 flips, Christopher and Jonathan didn't win or lose any amount.

Let H be the number of times the coin landed on Heads, and T be the number of times the coin landed on Tails.
Each flip can result in either Heads or Tails, so H + T = 20.
Christopher gives $2 for each Heads, so he gave away 2H dollars in total.
Jonathan gives $3 for each Tails, so he gave away 3T dollars in total.
Since they didn't win or lose any amount, we have 2H = 3T.
We also know that H + T = 20, so T = 20 - H.
Substituting this into 2H = 3T, we get 2H = 3(20 - H), which simplifies to 5H = 60, or H = 12.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Distance = Speed * Time
  Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph
  Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph
  Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  Let's call the distance between A and B as "d".
  Let's call the time it took Kevin to reach B from A as "t1".
  Let's call the time it took Kevin to return from B to A as "t2".

Solution:
  We know that: Distance = Speed * Time
  Therefore, d = 70 * t1  (Equation 1)
  Also, d = 90 * t2  (Equation 2)

  We also know that 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. 
  This means that at that time, he had already spent (t1 + t2 - 3) hours on his trip. 
  We can use this information to create another equation:

  70 = 90 * (t1 + t2 - 3) + 70   (Equation 3)

  Now we have three equations with three unknowns (d, t1, t2). We can solve for them simultaneously.

  From Equation 1, we get:
  t1 = d/70

  From Equation 2, we get:
  t2 = d/90

  Substituting these values in Equation 3, we get:
  70 = 90 * (d/70 + d/90 - 3) + 70
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  1 = d/1260
  Therefore, d = 1260

Action: Answer("E")

  - Distance = Rate x Time
  - Let d = distance from A to B
  - Let t1 = time it takes Kevin to travel from A to B at 70 mph
  - Let t2 = time it takes Kevin to travel from B to A at 90 mph
  - We know that t2 = t1 - 3, since he has 3 hours left in his trip when he is 70 miles away from B.
  - We also know that d = 70t1 (distance from A to B) and d = 90t2 (distance from B to A)

Solution:
  - Using d = 70t1 and d = 90t2, we can substitute t2 with t1 - 3 to get:
    70t1 = 90(t1 - 3)
    70t1 = 90t1 - 270
    20t1 = 270
    t1 = 13.5
  - We know that d = 70t1, so d = 70 x 13.5 = 945

    - d = 70t1 + 90t2
    - d = 70t1 + 90t1
    - d = 160t1
    - t1 = d/160
  - Substituting "t1" in the equation "t1 + t2 + 3 = d/70":
    - (d/160) + (d/160) + 3 = d/70
    - (2d/160) + (3*160/160) = d/70
    - (2d+480)/160 = d/70
    - 140d+42000 = 160d
    - 42000 = 20d
    - d = 2100
  - The distance between A and B is 2100 miles.

  (d-70)/90 = 3
  which can be simplified to:

  - Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. 
  - Kevin returned from B to A at a constant speed of 90 mph.
  - Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  - Let's assume the distance between A and B is "d". 

Approach:
  - Let's calculate the time it took for Kevin to travel from A to B. 
  - Let's assume the time Kevin took to return from B to A is "t". 
  - Then, the time Kevin took to travel from A to B is "t + 3". 
  - Using Distance = Rate x Time, we can form two equations with two unknowns (t and d). 

Equations:
  - d = 70(t + 3) (Distance traveled from A to B)
  - d = 90t + 70 (Distance traveled from B to A)

Solution:
  - Equate both equations for "d" and solve for "t":
    - 70(t + 3) = 90t + 70
    - 70t + 210 = 90t + 70
    - 20t = 140
    - t = 7
  - Substitute "t" in any of the two equations to find "d":
    - d = 90t + 70
    - d = 90(7) + 70
    - d = 700
  - Answer: The distance between A and B is 700 miles.

Response 8:
Knowledge: 
  - Distance = Speed × Time (for constant speed)
  - Let's assume that the distance between A and B is "d".
  - Let's assume that the time it takes to get from A to B at a speed of 70 mph is "t1".
  - Let's assume that the time it takes to get from B to A at a speed of 90 mph is "t2".
  - We know that t1 + t2 = total trip time.
  - We also know that 3 hours before the end of the trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. This means that he had already traveled (d-70) miles at that point.
Action: 
  - Let's use the formula Distance = Speed × Time to derive two equations for d, t1, and t2:
    - d = 70t1
    - d = 90t2
  - We can use the equation d = 70t1 to substitute for d in the equation d = 90t2:
    - 70t1 = 90t2
    - t1 = (9/7)t2
  - We also know that t1 + t2 = total trip time. Let's use this to derive an equation for t2:
    - t1 + t2 = t_total
    - (9/7)t2 + t2 = t_total
    - (16/7)t2 = t_total
    - t2 = (7/16)t_total
  - Now let's use the fact that he had already traveled (d - 70) miles 3 hours before the end of the trip, and the formula Distance = Speed × Time to derive another equation:
    - (d - 70) = 70(t1 - 3) + 90t2
    - (d - 70) = 70((9/7)t2 - 3) + 90t2
    - (d - 70) = (90/7)t2 - 210
    - (d - 70) = (90/7)((7/16)t_total) - 210
    - (d - 70) = (45/8)t_total - 210
  - We have three equations with three unknowns (d, t1, t2). Let's substitute t1 and t2 in terms of t_total and solve for d:
    - d = 70t1
    - d = 70((9/7)t2)
    - d = (630/7)t2
    - d = (630/7)((7/16)t_total)
    - d = (45/2)t_total - 630
  - Now we can substitute the given value of (d - 70) and solve for t_total:
    - (d - 70) = (45/2)t_total - 630
    - 70 = (45/2)t_total - (d - 630)
    - 70 = (45/2)t_total - (1/2)d + 630
    - (1/2)d = (45/2)t_total - 560
    - d = 45t_total - 1120
  - We know that t_total = t1 + t2. Let's substitute t1 and t2 in terms of t_total:
    - t1 = (9/7)t2
    - t2 = (7/16)t_total
    - t_total = t1 + t2
    - t_total = (9/7)t2 + (7/16)t_total
    - (7/16)t_total = (9/7)t2
    - t_total = (144/49)t2
  - Now we can substitute the expression for t_total in terms of t2 into the expression for d:
    - d = 45t_total - 1120
    - d = 45((144/49)t2) - 1120
    - d = (6480/49)t2 - 1120
  - We can now substitute this expression for d into the equation we derived earlier:
    - (d - 70) = (45/8)t_total - 210
    - ((6480/49)t2 - 70) = (45/8)((144/49)t2) - 210
    - ((6480/49)t2 - 70) = (1620/49)t2 - 210
    - (4860/49)t2 = 140
    - t2 = (49/4860)×140 = 7/27
  - Finally, we can substitute this value of t2 into the expression we derived earlier for d:
    - d = (6480/49)t2 - 1120
    - d = (6480/49)×(7/27) - 1120
    - d = 180

  B: 32456
  C: 76523
  D: 24567

Simplifying the above equation, we get:
2a = 2 + 7e
Since a is a digit, the only possible value for a is 1, and so we have:
e = (2/7) which is not possible as e is a digit.
Therefore, there is no such 5 digit number that satisfies the given condition.

  If we add 1 after it, the new number is "abcde1" and it is three times as large as the original number, "abcde", plus 1. 
  Therefore, we can write the following equation:
  10^4 * a + 10^3 * b + 10^2 * c + 10 * d + e + 1 = 3 * (10 * a + b + 10^2 * c + 10^3 * d + 10^4 * e + 1)
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  29999e = 2 * (10a + b - e) + 2999c
  This means that 29999e is an even number, so e must be either 0 or 5.
  If e = 0, then 2 * (10a + b) + 2999c = 0, which is impossible because the left-hand side is even and the right-hand side is odd.
  Therefore, e = 5, and we can rewrite the equation as:
  10a + b - 5 = (2999/2)c
  This means that (2999/2)c is an integer, so c must be a multiple of 2 and not equal to 0.
  From the answer choices, only option A satisfies these conditions:
  A: 42857

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Let's assume that there are "n" employees in the organization.

Knowledge:
  1. The organization has to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each employee.
  2. If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh.
  3. The contribution amount per employee before the increment is Rs. 6,00,000/n.
  4. The contribution amount per employee after the increment is Rs. (6,24,000/n) = Rs. (6,00,000/n + 60).
  
Calculation:
  6,24,000/n = 6,00,000/n + 60
  24,000/n = 60
  n = 400
  
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Let x be the number of employees in the organization.
If each employee contributed equally, they would contribute a total of Rs. 6 lakh. Therefore, each employee would contribute 6 lakh / x.
If each employee contributed Rs. 60 extra, they would contribute a total of Rs. 6.24 lakh. Therefore, each employee would contribute (6.24 lakh / x) = (6 lakh / x) + 60.
Simplifying the above equation, we get 0.24 lakh = 60,000, which means that 1 lakh = 250,000.
So, the above equation becomes (0.24 x 250000) = (60 x x), which simplifies to 60x = 60 x 4/1, and hence x = 240.
Therefore, there are 240 employees in the organization.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")  (The answer should be 240 which is not available in the options)
Response 2:
Let's assume that there are "n" employees in the organization.
The total amount collected from each employee is Rs. 6 lakh / n
When each employee contributes an extra Rs. 60, the total amount collected becomes Rs. 6.24 lakh. This can be represented as:
(n * (6 lakh / n + 60)) = 6.24 lakh

Solving the above equation:
6 lakh + 60n = 6.24 lakh
60n = 24,000
n = 400

Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 98 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Let the share of each nephew be x.  
Then each daughter will receive 4x and each son will receive 5x.  
Total number of people = 5 + 4 + 2 = 11.  
Therefore,  
5(5x) + 4(4x) + 2(x) = 8600  
25x + 16x + 2x = 8600/11  
43x = 780  
x = 18  
So each daughter will receive 4x = 4(18) = 72.  
Action: Answer("A") so the answer is Rs 400.

Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge:

  Actual value of the number = (Incorrect value of the number) * (Actual fraction) / (Incorrect fraction)
  Let the number be x.
  Incorrect fraction is 7/18 and its value is (7/18) * x.
  Actual fraction is 7/8 and its value is (7/8) * x.
  The student's answer differed from the actual one by 770, so we can write:
  (7/8)x - (7/18)x = 770
  Simplifying the above equation, we get:
  (35/72)x = 770
  x = (770 * 72) / 35
  x = 1584
Action: Answer("A")

(actual value) = (incorrect value) * (actual number) / (incorrect number)

x = 1584

Therefore, the answer is A: 1584.
